These should look like standard institutional safety features — professionally installed and maintained.

AMBULANCE BAY (if applicable): If a ground-level drop-off or ambulance bay area is visible, it should look clean, clearly marked with medical signage, well-lit, and organized — consistent with a teaching hospital entrance.


## 11. ISLAMIC ARCHITECTURAL INTEGRATION

This is the defining cultural design layer:

EXISTING GEOMETRIC SCREENS: The existing concrete mashrabiya screens on the campus are the heritage signature. They must be restored to gleaming white perfection. Their pattern (interlocking eight-point stars with cross-shaped voids) must be echoed AT MULTIPLE SCALES across the campus: (a) at full architectural scale on the existing screens themselves, (b) at medium scale on the NEW laser-cut decorative AC unit covers and security window screens, (c) at small scale on entrance door etchings and signage frame corners (if visible), and (d) at ground scale in the entrance plaza geometric paving pattern.

MASHRABIYA RHYTHM CONTINUITY: The rhythm of the screen perforations must visually harmonize with the rhythm of the vertical aluminum/painted fins on the adjacent renovated facade sections — creating a continuous visual rhythm that transitions from traditional (perforated concrete) to contemporary (solid painted fins) without a jarring break.

MUQARNAS (ONLY at existing canopy soffits): Where an entrance canopy already exists, its soffit may feature a contemporary reinterpretation of muqarnas (Islamic honeycomb vaulting) — executed as a relief panel in white finish. Do NOT add muqarnas elements to facades, walls, or areas where they would look out of context.

CALLIGRAPHY: The main entrance signage in Arabic must use a beautiful, prestigious Naskh calligraphy style — not a generic computer typeface. It must appear custom-designed and premium.

COURTYARD PRINCIPLES (where courtyards are visible): Apply Islamic garden design principles — geometry, symmetry, water, shade, and aromatic planting. The reflective water mirror, the symmetrical planters, the shade-providing trees, and the fragrant jasmine all reference the Chahar Bagh (four-garden) tradition.


## 12. REALISM, RENDERING CONSTRAINTS & MARKETING-GRADE VISUAL QUALITY

The output image MUST appear as:

A STUNNING, MARKETING-GRADE professional architectural photograph — the kind published on the cover of Architectural Digest, Dezeen, or ArchDaily. It must look like a REAL photograph taken on-site after renovation completion by the BEST architectural photographer in the Middle East, using the BEST equipment, at the PERFECT moment of golden-hour light. Not a render. Not a concept image. A breathtaking PHOTOGRAPH that makes the viewer stop scrolling and say "WOW."

⚠️ FRAME-LOCK REMINDER (REPEATED FOR EMPHASIS) ⚠️
The output image MUST maintain the EXACT SAME framing, cropping, field of view, zoom level, and boundaries as the input photograph. If the building is partially cropped in the input, it MUST remain partially cropped in the EXACT SAME WAY in the output. Do NOT extend, outpaint, widen, or shift the viewport by ANY amount. The input frame is LOCKED. Output dimensions = Input dimensions. Every pixel position maps 1:1.

MARKETING-GRADE PHOTOGRAPHIC QUALITIES:
• GOLDEN-HOUR CINEMATIC LIGHTING — warm, directional sunlight from the west (25–35° sun angle) that makes every surface glow with richness and warmth
• ENHANCED CONTRAST — slightly boosted contrast beyond typical photography, pushing the darks deeper and the highlights warmer to create a punchy, magazine-quality tonal range
• RICH COLOR SATURATION — colors must be 15-20% more saturated than ordinary photography — the ivory walls glow warmer, the navy fins appear deeper and more luxurious, the green vegetation is more vibrant and lush, the sky is more dramatically golden
• MATERIAL SHINE AND TEXTURE — every material must show exaggerated tactile quality: you should be able to FEEL the stone grain, SEE the metal sheen, SENSE the glass smoothness
• Physically accurate shadows — shadow direction consistent with a late-afternoon Cairo sun angle, shadows that are crisp and well-defined with warm fill-light in the shadow areas (not black voids)
• DRAMATIC SKY — warm gradient from deep blue at zenith through pale blue to rich golden-peach near the horizon, with optional thin wispy cirrus clouds for texture. The sky must be BEAUTIFUL enough to be a photograph on its own
• Natural atmospheric haze consistent with Nasr City, Cairo (slight warm haze softening distant objects, adding atmospheric depth)
• DEEP DEPTH OF FIELD — tack-sharp from foreground through mid-ground, with the slightest softening in the far background to create cinematic depth
• Photographic grain consistent with an ISO 100 full-frame medium-format sensor (extremely fine, almost invisible grain)
• TONAL RICHNESS — the image should have at least 3 distinct tonal zones: bright highlights (sky, sunlit walls), rich midtones (shaded walls, vegetation), and deep shadows (pilotis, recessed areas) — creating a three-dimensional, sculptural quality

PROHIBITED EFFECTS: No artificial glow effects, no lens flares, no bloom, no heavy vignetting, no HDR tonemapping artifacts, no oversaturation to the point of unrealism, no artificial fog, no dramatic storm clouds, no reflection mapping errors, no levitating objects, no transparent walls, no visible wireframes, no duplicated textures, no warped geometry, no cartoon effects, no watercolor effects, no painterly effects. The enhanced visual quality must feel NATURAL and PHOTOGRAPHIC — not processed or filtered.

MATERIAL ACCURACY (ENHANCED FOR MARKETING): All materials must obey real-world physics BUT rendered at their most BEAUTIFUL possible state. Plaster must look like the finest plaster ever applied (subtle surface texture catching raking golden light, warm matte sheen with micro-variations). Metal must look like the most expensive metal (rich reflections, perfectly oriented brushed grain, satin anodized depth that suggests quality). Glass must look like premium architectural glass (warm sky reflections blended with green canopy reflections, subtle blue-green tint, sharp mullion shadows, the sense of looking into a well-lit interior beyond). Stone must look like quarried Egyptian limestone at its peak (warm fossil inclusions catching the light, subtle crystalline sparkle, the sense of geological WEIGHT and PERMANENCE). Water must be MIRROR-PERFECT (undistorted building reflections, sky reflections, the faintest edge ripple for realism). Plants must look IMPOSSIBLY LUSH and HEALTHY (every leaf catching the golden light with subsurface scattering, warm green tones, the sense of abundant life and careful cultivation). Decorative screens must look like museum-quality metalwork (precise laser-cut edges catching thin golden highlights, geometric patterns casting precise shadow artwork on adjacent surfaces).

PEOPLE AND VEHICLES: REMOVE ALL people, cars, motorcycles, bicycles, and any moving/parked objects. The scene must be completely depopulated. Replace removed elements with the underlying architecture, landscape, or paving that would logically exist behind them. The scene should feel early-morning pristine — the golden hour before the campus awakens — creating a sense of SERENITY, SPACE, and ARCHITECTURAL PURITY.


## 13. STRUCTURAL PRESERVATION RULES

ABSOLUTE NON-NEGOTIABLE CONSTRAINTS — VIOLATION OF ANY OF THESE RULES INVALIDATES THE OUTPUT:

• DO NOT add any floors to the building. Maintain the EXACT number of visible stories.
• DO NOT remove any floors from the building.
• DO NOT change the building's overall height, width, or depth proportions.
• DO NOT alter the building's footprint or plan shape.
• DO NOT change the structural grid spacing (column-to-column dimension).
• DO NOT relocate, add, or remove structural columns, beams, or walls.
• DO NOT change the window grid placement — window positions must remain on the SAME structural grid coordinates as the original photograph.
• DO NOT alter the campus road layout, building positions relative to each other, or the overall site plan.
• DO NOT demolish any building, wing, or section — ALL existing structures must remain and be upgraded.
• DO NOT change the building from a rectilinear form to a curved or organic form.
• DO NOT add tall towers, domes, minarets, or any vertical elements that were not present in the original photograph.
• DO NOT add an entrance, door, or gateway where none exists in the original photograph.
• DO NOT change the concrete structural system — every slab edge, beam depth, and column width remains IDENTICAL.
• DO NOT change the camera angle, perspective, or viewpoint from the original photograph.
• DO NOT change the landscape layout — tree positions, path routes, and planter locations are FIXED.
• ALL trees, hedges, and structural planting remain in their EXACT original positions.
• The building SILHOUETTE against the sky must remain IDENTICAL to the original photograph.

⚠️ FRAME-LOCK RULE (FINAL REPETITION — MOST CRITICAL RULE) ⚠️
• DO NOT change the image dimensions, framing, cropping, or boundaries from the input photograph.
• DO NOT extend the image beyond the original photo edges.
• DO NOT zoom out to show more of the building.
• DO NOT shift the camera to reveal hidden parts of the building.
• DO NOT attempt to "complete" a building that is partially cropped at the frame edge.
• If the building is cut off at the left edge of the input photo, it MUST remain cut off at the EXACT same position in the output.
• If the building is cut off at the right edge, top edge, or bottom edge, it stays cut off IDENTICALLY.
• The output image is a 1:1 pixel-mapped transformation of the input — same width, same height, same viewport, same everything. ONLY the SURFACE QUALITY of what's visible changes.

ONLY the following SURFACE-LEVEL modifications are permitted:
Wall paint/plaster quality, facade colors, surface textures, decorative screen additions (over AC units, over security bars), column ornamental bands, slab edge cornices, window surrounds, building base plinth treatment, parapet coping, rainwater pipe refinishing, window glass cleanliness, window frame refinishing, existing entrance portal restoration, existing canopy enhancement, lighting fixture additions, landscape visual quality improvement, new landscape features in EMPTY areas only (water features, seating, fountains, shade structures, benches, waste bins, bicycle racks, flagpoles, digital kiosks, sculptural art, geometric paving patterns, planter boxes), signage restoration and standardization, paving condition improvement, and surface-level architectural detailing. All changes are ADDITIVE SURFACE TREATMENTS applied to the EXISTING structural skeleton — the skin changes, the bones stay IDENTICAL. Pursue the ABSOLUTE MAXIMUM possible improvement within these constraints — every pixel of the output should be more beautiful, more luxurious, and more architecturally refined than the input. The final result must establish this building as THE LANDMARK OF AL-AZHAR UNIVERSITY — the most photographed, most admired, most iconic structure on the entire campus. A building that stops traffic. A building that makes the news. A building that defines what Islamic medical education looks like in the 21st century. FRAME = LOCKED. STRUCTURE = FROZEN. SURFACES = MAXIMALLY UPGRADED TO LANDMARK STATUS.


## 14. MARKETING-GRADE VISUAL RICHNESS CHECKLIST

Before finalizing the output image, ensure ALL of the following visual richness elements are present. These are what separate a "good" architectural renovation image from a STUNNING, MARKETING-GRADE, WORLD-CLASS image worthy of a CAMPUS LANDMARK — the building that defines Al-Azhar University's visual identity:

✅ WARM GOLDEN LIGHT bathes all sun-facing surfaces, creating a honey-gold luminosity on ivory walls
✅ DEEP, RICH SHADOWS in all recessed areas (window reveals, pilotis, under canopies) — not black, but deep warm-grey with subtle detail visible
✅ GEOMETRIC SHADOW PATTERNS from mashrabiya screens and decorative metal screens projected onto adjacent walls and ground — sharp, beautiful, and architecturally dramatic

## 1. INTERIOR TRANSFORMATION OBJECTIVE

You are receiving a real photograph of an INTERIOR space within the Faculty of Medicine – Al-Azhar University campus. Your task is to produce a photorealistic image showing this EXACT same interior space after a high-quality renovation has been completed. The output must look like a REAL photograph of a REAL completed interior renovation — not a concept render, not a CGI scene.

CRITICAL PRESERVATION MANDATE:

You MUST preserve the following elements EXACTLY as they appear in the input photograph — with ZERO deviation:

• The EXACT camera angle, viewpoint, and perspective.
• The EXACT room dimensions, ceiling height, and spatial volume.
• The EXACT structural elements — all columns, beams, walls, slab soffits, stairwells, and structural openings remain in their IDENTICAL positions.
• The EXACT door and window positions — no doors or windows added, removed, or relocated.
• The EXACT corridor widths, stairwell dimensions, and circulation layout.
• The EXACT ceiling structure type — if it is an exposed concrete slab, it remains so; if it has a suspended ceiling, it remains so.
• The EXACT floor level — no raising, lowering, or stepping modifications.

VARIABLE REMOVAL MANDATE:
Remove ALL people, staff, students, visitors, portable equipment, loose items, scattered papers, temporary posters, and any transient objects from the scene. Replace removed elements with the underlying walls, floors, or architectural surfaces that would logically exist behind them.

What you ARE allowed to do:
ONLY surface-level interior improvements: upgrading wall finishes, improving floor finishes, upgrading ceiling treatments, improving lighting fixtures, cleaning and restoring all surfaces, adding architectural details, improving signage, concealing exposed pipes/wires, and enhancing material quality — all applied to the EXISTING structural shell.


## 2. INTERIOR IDENTITY DIRECTION

The renovated interiors must communicate:

(A) WORLD-CLASS MEDICAL INSTITUTION: Clinical precision, absolute cleanliness, bright and well-lit spaces, organized circulation. Every surface must suggest a premium hospital or medical research facility.

(B) AL-AZHAR SCHOLARLY PRESTIGE: Dignified materials, warm undertones in the color palette, and selective Islamic geometric accents (e.g., a geometric floor pattern at a lobby threshold, a decorative screen partition, a calligraphic wall panel).

(C) CONTEMPORARY ACADEMIC QUALITY: Modern lighting, clean lines, professional wayfinding signage, and a consistent material palette throughout all visible spaces.


## 3. WALL TREATMENT

EXISTING PAINTED WALLS: Upgrade ALL interior walls to a pristine, freshly-painted condition. Lower wall zone (0–1200mm from floor): durable, matte washable paint in a slightly darker warm tone (Hex #D4C5A9 — warm sand). Upper wall zone (1200mm to ceiling): clean matte paint in off-white / warm ivory (Hex #F5F0E8). This two-tone treatment is practical for a medical institution (the lower darker band hides scuff marks) and looks refined.

WALL JUNCTIONS: All wall/ceiling and wall/floor junctions must have clean, sharp edges. No visible cracks, no peeling paint, no damp stains, no mold, no graffiti marks, no tape residue, no poster marks. Absolute perfection.

FEATURE WALLS (lobbies and prominent corridors): At key locations (entrance lobbies, administrative reception areas, stairwell landings), add ONE decorative accent wall panel — either a subtle Islamic geometric pattern in a laser-cut metal panel (Deep Navy, backlit with warm LED), or a polished stone panel (cream marble) with the Al-Azhar logo or a medical-themed relief.

EXPOSED PIPES AND CONDUITS: All visible pipes, cable trays, electrical conduits, and service ducts on walls must be concealed behind clean, flush-mounted cover panels painted to match the adjacent wall color. No exposed services of any kind.


## 4. FLOOR TREATMENT

EXISTING TILE FLOORS: If the existing floor is tile (ceramic, terrazzo, stone), upgrade it to look freshly polished, crack-free, and gleaming. All grout lines must be clean and consistent. No chipped tiles, no mismatched tiles, no staining, no discoloration.

EXISTING STONE FLOORS: If the floor is natural stone (granite, marble, limestone), polish it to a mirror sheen. Remove all scratches and stains. All joints must be tight and clean.

EXISTING CONCRETE FLOORS: If the floor is exposed concrete or cement, seal it with a polished concrete finish — smooth, reflective, dust-free, and uniformly colored (medium grey).

FLOOR PATTERNS: At major circulation junctions and lobby spaces, enhance the floor with a subtle geometric border pattern using contrasting stone inlays — forming a simplified Islamic star tessellation. This echoes the campus exterior mashrabiya patterns and creates visual continuity between inside and outside.

TRANSITION STRIPS: At all door thresholds and material change points, show clean brushed stainless steel transition strips — flush-mounted, precise, and professional.


## 5. CEILING TREATMENT

EXISTING SUSPENDED CEILINGS: If the ceiling has acoustic tiles or plasterboard, make them look fresh, white, uniform, and free of any stains, sagging panels, or missing tiles. All ceiling grid lines must be straight and consistent.

EXISTING EXPOSED CONCRETE CEILINGS: Clean and seal the concrete surface. Apply a thin white mineral coating that preserves the concrete's texture while making it bright and clean. All beam edges must be crisp.

LIGHTING FIXTURES IN CEILING: Replace all visible outdated fluorescent tube fixtures with modern recessed LED panel lights (600mm × 600mm, 4000K neutral white, even diffused light). If the ceiling type doesn't allow recessing, show linear LED strip fixtures (slim profile, surface-mounted, white housing) aligned with the room's long axis for a clean, directional effect.

CEILING-MOUNTED SERVICES: All visible sprinkler heads, smoke detectors, and speakers must appear as clean, modern, white-painted units — professionally positioned and aligned.


## 6. LIGHTING

GENERAL ILLUMINATION: The entire interior must appear brightly and evenly lit with 4000K neutral white LED lighting — no dark corners, no flickering, no uneven patches, no yellow-cast from old fluorescent tubes. The lighting must suggest a modern medical institution: bright, clean, and comfortable.

ACCENT LIGHTING: At feature walls, decorative panels, and signage — add targeted warm-white (3000K) accent spotlights or LED strip backlighting to highlight architectural features and create visual hierarchy.

STAIRWELL LIGHTING: Stairwells must be brightly and uniformly lit from step-nose LED strips (embedded in each step tread for safety) and wall-wash fixtures at every landing.

CORRIDOR LIGHTING: Long corridors receive evenly-spaced recessed or surface-mounted linear LED fixtures that create a continuous light line along the ceiling — providing uniform illumination and a sense of direction.

NATURAL LIGHT: Where windows or glass doors are visible, maximize the perception of natural daylight entering the space. Glass must be perfectly clean and transparent. Views through windows should show the upgraded exterior campus.


## 7. DOORS AND OPENINGS

EXISTING DOORS: All doors remain in their EXACT positions. Upgrade their appearance: if wood, make them look freshly varnished in a warm medium-tone wood finish. If metal, repaint them in the campus Deep Navy color with clean hardware. If glass, make them spotlessly clean.

DOOR HARDWARE: All handles, hinges, and locks must appear as modern, brushed stainless steel or brushed bronze — matching, consistent, and new.

DOOR SIGNAGE: All room/department signs must be standardized: brushed metal frames, bilingual (Arabic + English), clean modern typefaces, with the Al-Azhar logo. Medical departments may include a minimal Rod of Asclepius icon.


## 8. WAYFINDING AND SIGNAGE

All interior signage visible in the photograph must be upgraded to a unified design system:

• DIRECTIONAL SIGNS: Clean rectangular panels in brushed bronze frames, white background, Deep Navy text, bilingual (Arabic Naskh + English sans-serif).
• ROOM NUMBERS: Standardized metal numerals mounted on or beside doors.
• DEPARTMENT NAMES: Larger panels with the department name in both languages, potentially with a subtle Islamic border pattern as a frame.
• DIGITAL DISPLAYS: At major lobby spaces, add flat-panel digital display screens (in slim brushed metal frames) showing academic notices — replacing all temporary paper posters and tape-on flyers.

All temporary posters, handwritten signs, tape-on notices, and ad-hoc signage must be REMOVED and replaced with proper institutional signage.


## 9. FURNITURE AND FIXTURES
